<TD WIDTH="9%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="justify"> <P ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Item&nbsp;1.</B></FONT></P></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Legal Proceedings </B></FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">As of
December&nbsp;29, 2007, the end of the quarterly period covered by this report, the Company is subject to the various legal proceedings and claims discussed below, as well as certain other legal proceedings and claims that have not been fully
resolved and that have arisen in the ordinary course of business. In the opinion of management, the Company does not have a potential liability related to any current legal proceedings and claims that would individually or in the aggregate have a
material adverse effect on its financial condition or operating results. However, the results of legal proceedings cannot be predicted with certainty. Should the Company fail to prevail in any of these legal matters or should several of these legal
matters be resolved against the Company in the same reporting period, the operating results of a particular reporting period could be materially adversely affected. The Company settled certain matters during the first quarter of 2008 that did not
individually or in the aggregate have a material impact on the Company&#146;s results of operations. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Apple Computer, Inc. v. Burst.com,
Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company filed an action for declaratory judgment against defendant Burst.com, Inc. on January&nbsp;4, 2006 in the United
States District Court for the Northern District of California. The Company sought declaratory judgment that U.S. Patent Nos. 4,963,995, 5,164,839, 5,057,932 and 5,995,705 (&#147;Burst patents&#148;) are invalid and not infringed by the Company.
Burst filed an answer and counterclaim on April&nbsp;17, 2006 adding infringement allegations relating to U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,995,705. The Company counterclaimed for declaratory judgment that each of these patents is invalid, not infringed and
unenforceable. Burst alleged that the following Apple products and services infringe the four patents at issue: iTunes Store, iPod devices, iTunes software, iLife software (GarageBand, iMovie, iWeb) separately and in conjunction with the .Mac
service and Apple computers sold with or running iTunes or iLife. The Burst patents allegedly relate to methods and devices used for faster-than-real-time transmission of compressed audio and/or video files. The Court issued its claim construction
ruling on May&nbsp;8, 2007. The Company filed motions for summary judgment of invalidity on January&nbsp;4, 2007 and July&nbsp;13, 2007. The Court held a hearing on those pending motions on September&nbsp;18, 2007, and issued its ruling on
November&nbsp;8, 2007. The Company filed motions for summary judgment and partial summary judgment relating to enablement, indefiniteness and laches on October&nbsp;29, 2007. Trial was set for February&nbsp;26, 2008. The parties have reached a
settlement and the matter is concluded. Settlement of this matter did not have a material effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition or operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Bader v. Anderson, et al. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this purported shareholder derivative action against the
Company and each of its then current executive officers and members of its Board of Directors on May&nbsp;19, 2005 in Santa Clara County Superior Court asserting claims for breach of fiduciary duty, material misstatements and omissions and
violations of California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17200 (unfair competition). The complaint alleged that the Company&#146;s March&nbsp;14, 2005, proxy statement was false and misleading for failure to disclose certain information
relating to the Apple Computer, Inc. Performance Bonus Plan, which was approved by shareholders at the annual meeting held on April&nbsp;21, 2005. Plaintiff, who ostensibly brought suit on the Company&#146;s behalf, made no demand on the Board of
Directors and alleged that such demand was excused. The complaint sought injunctive and other relief for purported injury to the Company. On July&nbsp;27, 2005, plaintiff filed an amended complaint alleging that, in addition to the purported
derivative claims, adoption of the bonus plan and distribution of the proxy statement describing that plan also inflicted injury on her directly as an individual shareholder. On January&nbsp;10, 2006, the Court sustained defendants&#146; demurrer to
the amended complaint, with leave to amend. Plaintiff filed a second amended complaint on February&nbsp;7, 2006, and the Company filed a demurrer. After a hearing on June&nbsp;13, 2006, the Court sustained the demurrer without leave to amend as to
the non-director officers and with leave to amend as to the directors. On July&nbsp;24, 2006, plaintiff filed a third amended complaint, which purported to bring claims derivatively as well as directly on behalf of a class of common stockholders who
have been or will be harmed by virtue of the allegedly misleading proxy statement. In addition to reasserting prior causes of action, the third amended complaint included a claim that the Company violated the terms of the plan, and a claim for waste
related to restricted stock unit grants to certain officers in 2003 and 2004 and an option grant to the Company&#146;s CEO in January 2000. The Company filed a demurrer to the third amended complaint. On January&nbsp;30, 2007, the Court sustained
the Company&#146;s demurrer with leave to amend. On May&nbsp;8, 2007, plaintiff filed a fourth amended complaint. The Company filed a demurrer to the fourth amended complaint, which the Court sustained, without leave to amend, on October&nbsp;12,
2007. On October&nbsp;25, 2007, the Court entered a final judgment in favor of defendant and ordered the case dismissed with prejudice. On November&nbsp;26, 2007, plaintiff filed a notice of appeal. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">30 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Birdsong v. Apple Computer, Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">This action alleges that the Company&#146;s iPod music players, and the ear bud headphones sold with them, are inherently defective in design and are sold without adequate warnings concerning the
risk of noise-induced hearing loss by iPod users. The Birdsong action was initially filed on January&nbsp;30, 2006 in the United States District Court for the Western District of Louisiana asserting Louisiana causes of action on behalf of a
purported Louisiana class of iPod purchasers. A similar action<I> (Patterson v. Apple Computer, Inc.)</I> was filed on January&nbsp;31, 2006 in the United States District Court for the Northern District of California asserting California causes of
action on behalf of a purported class of all iPod purchasers within the four-year period before January&nbsp;31, 2006. The Birdsong action was transferred to the Northern District of California, and the Patterson action was dismissed. An amended
complaint was subsequently filed in Birdsong, dropping the Louisiana law-based claims and adding California law-based claims equivalent to those in Patterson. After the Company filed a motion to dismiss on November&nbsp;3, 2006, plaintiffs agreed
not to oppose the motion and filed a second amended complaint on January&nbsp;16, 2007. That complaint alleges California law-based claims for breaches of implied and express warranties, violations of California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code
&#167;17200 (unfair competition), California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17500 (false advertising), the Consumer Legal Remedies Act and negligent misrepresentation on behalf of a putative nationwide class and a Louisiana law-based
claim for redhibition for a Louisiana sub-class. On March&nbsp;1, 2007, the Company filed a motion to dismiss the California law-based claims, which was heard on June&nbsp;4, 2007. On December&nbsp;14, 2007, the Court issued an order granting the
Company&#146;s motion, with leave to amend the complaint. Plaintiffs filed a third amended complaint on January&nbsp;11, 2008. The Company&#146;s response to the third amended complaint is not yet due. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A similar complaint,<I> Royer-Brennan v. Apple Computer, Inc. and Apple Canada, Inc.,</I> was filed in Montreal, Quebec, Canada, on February&nbsp;1,
2006, seeking authorization to institute a class action on behalf of iPod purchasers in Quebec. At the request of plaintiffs&#146; counsel, the Court has postponed class certification proceedings in this action indefinitely. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Branning et al. v. Apple Computer, Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">Plaintiffs originally filed this purported class action in San Francisco County Superior Court on February&nbsp;17, 2005. The initial complaint alleged violations of California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17200 (unfair
competition) and violation of the Consumer Legal Remedies Act regarding a variety of purportedly unfair and unlawful conduct including, but not limited to, allegedly selling used computers as new and failing to honor warranties. Plaintiffs also
brought causes of action for misappropriation of trade secrets, breach of contract and violation of the Song-Beverly Consumer Warranty Act. Plaintiffs requested unspecified damages and other relief. On May&nbsp;9, 2005, the Court granted the
Company&#146;s motion to transfer the case to Santa Clara County Superior Court. On May&nbsp;2, 2005, plaintiffs filed an amended complaint adding two new named plaintiffs and three new causes of action including a claim for treble damages under the
Cartwright Act (California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;16700 et seq.) and a claim for false advertising. The Company filed a demurrer to the amended complaint, which the Court sustained in its entirety on November&nbsp;10, 2005. The
Court granted plaintiffs leave to amend and they filed an amended complaint on December&nbsp;29, 2005. Plaintiffs&#146; amended complaint added three plaintiffs and alleged many of the same factual claims as the previous complaints, such as alleged
selling of used equipment as new, alleged failure to honor warranties and service contracts for the consumer plaintiffs, and alleged fraud related to the opening of the Apple retail stores. Plaintiffs continued to assert causes of action for unfair
competition (&#167;17200), violations of the Consumer Legal Remedies Act, breach of contract, misappropriation of trade secrets, violations of the Cartwright Act, and alleged new causes of action for fraud, conversion, and breach of the implied
covenant of good faith and fair dealing. The Company filed a demurrer to the amended complaint on January&nbsp;31, 2006, which the Court sustained on March&nbsp;3, 2006 on sixteen of seventeen causes of action. Plaintiffs filed an amended complaint
adding one new plaintiff. The Company filed a demurrer, which was granted in part on September&nbsp;9, 2006. Plaintiffs filed a further amended complaint on September&nbsp;21, 2006. On October&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company filed an answer denying all
allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses. On November&nbsp;30, 2007, the Company filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings, which the Court denied. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>European Commission Investigation </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The European Commission is investigating certain matters relating
to the iTunes Stores in Europe. The European Commission had previously notified the Company that it was investigating claims made by Which?, a United Kingdom (&#147;U.K.&#148;) consumer association, that the Company is violating EU competition law
by charging more for online music in the U.K. than in Eurozone countries and preventing U.K. consumers from purchasing online music from the iTunes Stores for Eurozone countries. The Which? claims were originally lodged with the U.K. Office of Fair
Trading, which subsequently referred them to the European Commission. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">31 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On March&nbsp;30, 2007, the European Commission issued Statements of Objections to the major record
labels, Apple Inc. and iTunes S.&agrave;.r.l. In the Statements of Objections, the Commission challenges provisions in the agreements pursuant to which each major record company authorizes iTunes S.&agrave;.r.l. to distribute digital music downloads
through the iTunes Store. The Commission contends that, because of these provisions, residents of the European Economic Area are only permitted to buy music from the iTunes Store for the country that issued the customer&#146;s credit card. The
Commission contends that these provisions are territorial sales restrictions which violate Article 81 of the European Community Treaty. The Commission seeks fines and behavioral relief. The Company filed its responses to the Statements of Objections
on June&nbsp;20, 2007. A hearing on the Statements of Objections took place in Brussels, Belgium on September&nbsp;19, 2007. On January&nbsp;9, 2008, the Company announced that it planned to equalize the price of iTunes Store content throughout
Europe within six months. That same day, the Commission announced its intent to close the investigation. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Gordon v. Apple Computer, Inc.
</I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this purported class action on August&nbsp;31, 2006 in the United States District Court for the Northern District of
California, San Jose Division, on behalf of a purported nationwide class of consumers who purchased 65W Power Adapters for iBooks and Powerbooks between November 2002 and the present. The complaint alleges various problems with the 65W Adapter,
including fraying, sparking, and premature failure. Plaintiffs allege violations of California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17200 (unfair competition), the Consumer Legal Remedies Act, the Song-Beverly Consumer Warranty Act and breach
of warranties. The complaint seeks damages and equitable relief. The Company filed an answer on October&nbsp;20, 2006 denying the material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Harvey v. Apple Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed
this action on August&nbsp;6, 2007 in the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Texas, Marshall Division, alleging infringement by the Company of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;6,753,671 entitled &#147;Recharger for use with a portable
electronic device and which includes a proximally located light emitting device&#148; and U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;6,762,584 entitled &#147;Recharger for use with a portable electronic device and which includes a connector terminus for communicating
with rechargeable batteries contained within the device.&#148; The complaint seeks unspecified damages and other relief. The Company filed an answer on October&nbsp;12, 2007 denying all material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative
defenses. The Company also asserted counterclaims for declaratory judgment of non-infringement and invalidity. The Markman hearing is set for October&nbsp;28, 2009, and trial is scheduled for April&nbsp;5, 2010. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Honeywell International,&nbsp;Inc., et al.&nbsp;v. Apple Computer,&nbsp;Inc., et al. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiffs Honeywell International,&nbsp;Inc. and Honeywell Intellectual Properties,&nbsp;Inc. filed this action on October&nbsp;6, 2004 in the United States District Court in Delaware alleging
infringement by the Company and other defendants of U.S. Patent 5,280,371 entitled &#147;Directional Diffuser for a Liquid Crystal Display.&#148; Plaintiffs seek unspecified damages and other relief. The Company filed an answer on December&nbsp;21,
2004 denying all material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses. The Company has tendered the case to several liquid crystal display manufacturer suppliers. On May&nbsp;18, 2005 the Court stayed the case against the Company and the
other non-manufacturer defendants. Plaintiffs filed an amended complaint on November&nbsp;7, 2005 adding additional defendants and expanding the scope of the accused products. Given the stay, the Company&#146;s response to the amended complaint is
not yet due. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>In re Apple Computer, Inc. Derivative Litigation (formerly Karant v. Jobs, et al. and Related Actions) (Federal Action)
</I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On June&nbsp;30, 2006, a putative derivative action captioned <I>Karant v. Jobs, et. al.</I>, was filed in the United States District
Court for the Northern District of California, San Jose Division. A number of related actions were filed in the subsequent weeks and have been consolidated into a single action captioned <I>In re Apple Computer, Inc. Derivative Litigation</I>,
Master File No. C-06-04128-JF before the Hon. Jeremy Fogel. The actions were filed after the Company&#146;s announcement on June&nbsp;29, 2006 that an internal investigation had discovered irregularities related to the issuance of certain stock
option grants made between 1997 and 2001, that a special committee of the Company&#146;s outside directors had retained independent counsel to perform an investigation and that the Company had informed the Securities and Exchange Commission. The
action purports to assert claims on behalf of the Company against </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">32 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">several current and former executive officers and members of the Board of Directors alleging improper backdating of stock option grants to maximize certain
defendants&#146; profits, failing to properly account for and take tax deductions for those grants, insider trading, and issuing false financial statements. The Company is named as a nominal defendant. The consolidated complaint alleges various
causes of action under federal and California law, including claims for unjust enrichment, breach of fiduciary duty, violation of the California Corporations Code, abuse of control, gross mismanagement, rescission, constructive fraud and waste of
corporate assets, as well as claims under Sections 10(b), 14(a) and 20(a) of the Securities Exchange Act. Plaintiffs seek damages, disgorgement, restitution and imposition of a constructive trust. A Consolidated Shareholder Derivative Complaint was
filed on December&nbsp;18, 2006, and a First&nbsp;Amended Shareholder Derivative Complaint was filed on March&nbsp;6, 2007. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss on April&nbsp;20, 2007, which was heard on September&nbsp;7, 2007. On November&nbsp;19,
2007, the Court granted the defendants&#146; motion to dismiss with leave to amend. Plaintiffs filed an amended complaint on December&nbsp;19, 2007. Defendants filed motions to dismiss the amended complaint on January 25, 2008. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On June&nbsp;12, 2007, the Company&#146;s Board of Directors approved a resolution appointing a Special Litigation Committee to make all decisions
relating to options litigation. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>In re Apple Computer, Inc. Derivative Litigation (formerly Plumbers and Pipefitters v. Jobs, et al. and
Related Actions) (State Action); Boston Retirement Board v. Apple Computer, Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On July&nbsp;5, 2006, a putative derivative action
captioned <I>Plumbers and Pipefitters v. Jobs, et. al.</I>, was filed in California Superior Court for the County of Santa Clara. A number of related actions were filed in the subsequent weeks, and have been consolidated into a single action
captioned <I>In re Apple Computer, Inc. Derivative Litigation</I>, No.&nbsp;1:06CV066692, assigned to the Hon. Joseph Huber. These actions purport to assert claims on behalf of the Company against several current and former executive officers and
members of the Board of Directors alleging improper backdating of stock option grants to maximize certain defendants&#146; profits, failing to properly account for and take tax deductions for those grants and issuing false financial statements. The
Company is named as a nominal defendant. A consolidated complaint was filed on October&nbsp;5, 2006, alleging a variety of causes of action under California law, including claims for unjust enrichment, breach of fiduciary duty, violation of the
California Corporations Code, abuse of control, accounting, constructive trust, rescission, deceit, gross mismanagement and waste of corporate assets. On December&nbsp;7, 2006, the Court granted the Company&#146;s motion to stay these actions.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On November&nbsp;3, 2006, the Boston Retirement Board, a purported shareholder, filed a petition for writ of mandate against the Company
in California Superior Court for the County of Santa Clara County (<I>Boston Retirement Board v. Apple Computer Inc.</I>). The petition sought to compel the Company to allow inspection of certain corporate records relating to the Company&#146;s
option practices and the Special Committee&#146;s investigation. On January&nbsp;16, 2007, the Company filed a demurrer to the petition. The Court&nbsp;entered an order overruling the demurrer on March&nbsp;13, 2007. The Company filed its answer to
the petition on April&nbsp;5, 2007. The trial took place on September&nbsp;24, 2007. The Court granted the petition for inspection but narrowed the scope of the records to be produced. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>In re Apple iPod Nano Products Liability Litigation (formerly Wimmer v. Apple Computer, Inc.; Moschella, et al., v. Apple Computer, Inc.</I>; <I>Calado, et al. v. Apple Computer, Inc.</I>;
<I>Kahan, et al., v. Apple Computer, Inc</I>.; <I>Jennings, et al., v. Apple Computer, Inc.</I>; <I>Rappel v. Apple Computer, Inc.</I>; <I>Mayo v. Apple Computer, Inc.</I>; <I>Valencia v. Apple Computer, Inc.</I>; <I>Williamson v. Apple Computer,
Inc.</I>; <I>Sioson v. Apple Computer, Inc.</I> </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Beginning on October&nbsp;19, 2005, eight complaints were filed in various United States
District Courts and two complaints were filed in California State Court alleging that the Company&#146;s iPod nano was defectively designed so that it scratches excessively during normal use, rendering the screen unreadable. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The federal actions were coordinated in the United States District Court for the Northern District of California and assigned to the Hon. Ronald Whyte
pursuant to an April&nbsp;17, 2006 order of the Judicial Panel on Multidistrict Litigation. Plaintiffs filed a First Consolidated and Amended Master Complaint on September&nbsp;21, 2006, alleging violations of California and other states&#146;
consumer protection and warranty laws and claiming unjust enrichment. The Master Complaint alleges two putative plaintiff classes: (1)&nbsp;all U.S. residents (excluding California residents) who purchased an iPod nano that was not manufactured or
designed using processes necessary to ensure normal resistance to scratching of the screen; and (2)&nbsp;all iPod nano purchasers other than U.S. residents who purchased an iPod nano that was not manufactured or designed using processes necessary to
ensure normal resistance to scratching of the screen. The Company answered the Master Complaint on November&nbsp;20, 2006. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">33 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The two California State Court actions were coordinated on May&nbsp;4, 2006, and assigned to the Hon.
Carl West in Los Angeles Superior Court. Plaintiffs filed a Consolidated Amended Class Action Complaint on June&nbsp;8, 2006, alleging violations of California state consumer protection, unfair competition, false advertising and warranty laws and
claiming unjust enrichment. The Consolidated Complaint alleges a putative plaintiff class of all California residents who own an iPod nano containing a manufacturing defect that results in the nano being susceptible to excessive scratching. The
Company answered the Consolidated Amended Complaint on October&nbsp;6, 2006. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Two similar complaints, <I>Carpentier v. Apple Canada,
Inc</I>., and <I>Royer-Brennan v. Apple Computer, Inc. and Apple Canada, Inc</I>. were filed in Montreal, Quebec, Canada on October&nbsp;27, 2005 and November&nbsp;9, 2005, respectively, seeking authorization to institute class actions on behalf of
iPod nano purchasers in Quebec. The Royer-Brennan file was stayed in May 2006 in favor of the Carpentier file. A similar complaint, <I>Mund v. Apple Canada Inc. and Apple Computer, Inc.</I>, was filed in Ontario, Canada on January&nbsp;9, 2006
seeking authorization to institute a class action on behalf of iPod nano purchasers in Canada. Apple Canada Inc. and Apple Computer, Inc. have served Notices of Intent to Defend. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Individual Networks, LLC v. Apple, Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this action against
the Company on April&nbsp;24, 2007 in the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Texas, Marshall Division, alleging infringement of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;7,117,516, entitled &#147;Method and System for Providing a Customized Media
List.&#148; Plaintiff alleges certain features of the iTunes store infringe the patent. The complaint seeks unspecified damages and other relief. The Company filed an answer on July&nbsp;2, 2007, denying all material allegations and asserting
numerous affirmative defenses. The Company also asserted counterclaims for declaratory judgment of non-infringement and invalidity, as well as a counterclaim against Individual Networks LLC for infringement of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,724,567. The
Markman hearing is set for October&nbsp;8, 2008, and trial is scheduled for November&nbsp;9, 2009. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Intertainer, Inc. v. Apple Computer,
Inc., et al. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this action on December&nbsp;29, 2006 in the United States District Court for the Eastern District of
Texas, Marshall Division, alleging infringement by the Company and others of U.S. Patent number 6,925,469 entitled &#147;Digital Entertainment Service Platform.&#148; The complaint sought unspecified damages and other relief. The Company filed an
answer on February&nbsp;21, 2007 denying all material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses. The Company also asserted counterclaims for declaratory judgment of non-infringement and invalidity. The parties have reached a settlement
and the matter is concluded. Settlement of this matter did not have a material effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition or operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Lenzi v. Apple Canada, Inc.; Wolfe v. Apple Computer, Inc. and Apple Canada, Inc.; Hirst v. Apple Canada, Inc.; Hamilton v. Apple Computer, Inc. and Apple Canada, Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed a purported class action on June&nbsp;7, 2005, in Superior Court, in Montreal, Quebec, Canada allegedly on behalf of Quebec customers
claiming false advertising and breach of warranty relating to iPod battery life. Plaintiff sought authorization to institute a class action on behalf of Generations 1, 2 and 3 iPod owners in Quebec. On February&nbsp;2, 2006, the Court dismissed
plaintiff&#146;s motion for authorization to institute a class action. Plaintiff has appealed this ruling. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Two similar complaints relative
to iPod battery life, <I>Wolfe v. Apple</I> and <I>Hirst v. Apple</I>, were filed in Toronto, Ontario, Canada on August&nbsp;15, 2005 and September&nbsp;12, 2005, respectively. Counsel subsequently amended the complaint, now called <I>Waddell vs.
Apple</I>. The Waddell lawsuit is brought on behalf of all Canadian purchasers other than Quebec purchasers. On January&nbsp;17, 2006, the Company filed its statement of defence to the Waddell complaint. In addition, a similar complaint regarding
iPod battery life, <I>Hamilton v. Apple Computer, Inc. and Apple Canada, Inc.</I> was filed in Calgary, Alberta, Canada on October&nbsp;5, 2005, purportedly on behalf of all purchasers of iPods in Alberta, Canada. The complaint was served on
September&nbsp;27, 2006. The Company has reached a settlement of this matter and the parties have requested preliminary court approval for the settlement. Settlement of this matter will not have a material effect on the Company&#146;s financial
condition or operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Macadam&nbsp;v. Apple Computer,&nbsp;Inc.; Santos v. Apple Computer, Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Macadam action was filed in late 2002 in Santa Clara County Superior Court asserting various causes of action including breach of contract, fraud,
negligent and intentional interference with economic relationship, negligent misrepresentation, trade libel, unfair competition and false advertising. The complaint requested unspecified damages and other relief. The Company filed an answer on
December&nbsp;3, 2004 denying all allegations and asserting numerous defenses. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">34 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On October&nbsp;1, 2003, Macadam was deauthorized as an Apple reseller. Macadam filed a motion for a
temporary order to reinstate it as a reseller, which the Court denied. The Court denied Macadam&#146;s motion for a preliminary injunction on December&nbsp;19, 2003. On December&nbsp;6, 2004, Macadam filed for Chapter 11 bankruptcy in the Northern
District of California, which placed a stay on the litigation as to Macadam. The Company filed a claim in the bankruptcy proceedings on February&nbsp;16, 2005. The Macadam bankruptcy case was converted to Chapter 7 (liquidation) on April&nbsp;29,
2005. The Company has reached a settlement of Macadam&#146;s claims against the Company with the Chapter 7 Bankruptcy Trustee. The Bankruptcy Court approved the settlement on July&nbsp;17, 2006 over the objection of Tom Santos, Macadam&#146;s
principal. Santos appealed the ruling approving the settlement, but the District Court denied the appeal. Santos has appealed to the Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On December&nbsp;19, 2005, Tom Santos filed a Fifth Amended Complaint on his own behalf (not on behalf of Macadam) alleging fraud, violations of California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17200 (unfair
competition), California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17500 (false advertising) and the Consumer Legal Remedies Act. The Company filed a demurrer to Santos&#146; amended complaint and a special motion to strike the defamation cause of
action on January&nbsp;20, 2006. The Court sustained the demurrer in part but denied the special motion to strike. Santos filed a Sixth Amended Complaint on July&nbsp;14, 2006. The Company filed a demurrer, which was sustained on September&nbsp;9,
2006. Santos filed a Seventh Amended Complaint in late September 2006. The Company filed a motion to strike, which was granted in part and denied in part on December&nbsp;15, 2006. Santos filed an Eighth Amended Complaint on January&nbsp;29, 2007.
The Company filed a demurrer, which was heard on May&nbsp;7, 2007. The court sustained the demurrer, and Santos filed a Ninth Amended Complaint on July&nbsp;11, 2007. The Company filed a demurrer, which was overruled. The Company&#146;s answer to
the Ninth Amended Complaint is not yet due. The Company also filed a cross complaint against Santos on January&nbsp;20, 2006 alleging violations of California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17200 and California Penal Code &#167;502,
fraud and deceit and breach of contract. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Mediostream, Inc. v. Acer America Corp. et al. </I></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this action against the Company, Acer America Corp., Dell, Inc. and Gateway, Inc. on August&nbsp;28, 2007 in the United States District
Court for the Eastern District of Texas, Marshall Division, alleging infringement of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;7,009,655, entitled &#147;Method and System for Direct Recording of Video Information onto a Disk Medium.&#148; An amended complaint was served
on November&nbsp;7, 2007. The amended complaint seeks unspecified damages and other relief. On January 25, 2008, the Company filed an answer to the complaint denying all material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses and also filed
a motion to transfer the case to the Northern District of California. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>OPTi Inc. v. Apple Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this action against the Company on January&nbsp;16, 2007 in the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Texas, Marshall
Division, alleging infringement of U.S. Patent Nos. 5,710,906, 5,813,036 and 6,405,291, all entitled &#147;Predictive Snooping of Cache Memory for Master-Initiated Accesses.&#148; The complaint seeks unspecified damages and other relief. The Company
filed an answer on April&nbsp;17, 2007 denying all material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses. The Company also asserted counterclaims for declaratory judgment of non-infringement and invalidity. The Markman hearing is set for
November&nbsp;26, 2008, and trial is scheduled for April&nbsp;6, 2009. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Quantum Technology Management, Ltd. v. Apple Computer, Inc. </I>
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this action on December&nbsp;21, 2005 in the United States District Court for the District of Maryland against the Company
and Fingerworks, Ltd., alleging infringement of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,730,165 entitled &#147;Time Domain Capacitive Field Detector.&#148; The complaint seeks unspecified damages and other relief. On May&nbsp;11, 2006, Quantum filed an amended
complaint adding Cypress Semiconductor/MicroSystems, Inc. as a defendant. On July&nbsp;31, 2006, the Company filed an answer denying all material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses and also filed counterclaims for
non-infringement and invalidity. On November&nbsp;30, 2006, plaintiff filed a reply to the Company&#146;s counterclaims and a More Definite Statement. A Markman hearing was held on May&nbsp;16, 2007. On June&nbsp;7, 2007, the Court issued a claim
construction ruling, and also issued an order invalidating six of plaintiff&#146;s asserted patent claims in response to the Company&#146;s motion for partial summary judgment of invalidity. On November&nbsp;28, 2007, the Company filed a motion for
summary judgment for non-infringement and invalidity, and a motion for summary judgment related to Quantum&#146;s state-law claims. On December&nbsp;27, 2007, Quantum filed a motion for summary judgment for infringement on one patent claim. Trial is
scheduled for May&nbsp;19, 2008. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">35 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Saito Shigeru Kenchiku Kenkyusho (Shigeru Saito Architecture Institute) v. iPod; Apple Japan Inc. v.
Shigeru Saito Architecture Institute </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff&nbsp;Saito filed a petition in the Japan Customs Office in Tokyo on January&nbsp;23,
2007 alleging infringement by the Company of Japanese&nbsp;Patent No.&nbsp;3852854, entitled &#147;Touch Operation Input Device and Electronic Parts Thereof.&#148; The petition sought an order barring the importation into Japan of fifth generation
iPods and second generation iPod nanos. The Customs Office held a hearing on March&nbsp;22, 2007. The Customs Office rejected the petition to bar importation and dismissed plaintiff&#146;s case. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Apple Japan, Inc. filed a Declaratory Judgment action against Saito on February&nbsp;6, 2007 in the Tokyo District Court, seeking a declaration that the
&#145;854 patent is invalid and not infringed. Saito filed a Counter Complaint for infringement seeking damages. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>SP Technologies LLC v.
Apple Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this action against the Company on August&nbsp;2, 2007 in the United States District Court for the Eastern
District of Texas, Marshall Division, alleging infringement of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;6,784,873 entitled &#147;Method and Medium for Computer Readable Keyboard Display Incapable of User Termination.&#148; The complaint seeks unspecified damages and
other relief. The Company filed an answer on October&nbsp;23, 2007 denying all material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses. The Company also asserted counterclaims for declaratory judgment of non-infringement and invalidity. The
Markman hearing is set for September&nbsp;18, 2008, and trial is scheduled for June&nbsp;1, 2009. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>St-Germain v. Apple Canada, Inc. </I>
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this case in Montreal, Quebec, Canada, on August&nbsp;5, 2005, seeking authorization to institute a class action for the
refund by the Company of the Canadian Private Copying Levy that was applied to the iPod purchase price in Quebec between December&nbsp;12, 2003 and December&nbsp;14, 2004 but later declared invalid by the Canadian Court. The Company has completed a
refund program for this levy. A class certification hearing took place January&nbsp;13, 2006. On February&nbsp;24, 2006, the Court granted class certification and notice was published during the last week of March 2006. The trial was conducted on
October&nbsp;15 and 16, 2007. On January&nbsp;11, 2008, the Court issued a ruling in plaintiff&#146;s favor. The Court ruled that despite the Company&#146;s good faith efforts with the levy refund program, the Company must pay the amount claimed,
and that the class is comprised of 20,000 persons who purchased an iPod in Quebec between December&nbsp;12, 2003 and December&nbsp;14, 2004. The Court ordered the Company to submit a statement of account showing the amount received by the Canadian
Private Copying Collective, and the amount that has already been paid to class members in Quebec under the Company&#146;s levy refund program. The Court also ordered the parties to submit further briefing regarding the collective recovery award by
February&nbsp;23, 2008. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Texas MP3 Technologies Ltd v. Apple Inc. et al. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this action against the Company and other defendants on February&nbsp;16, 2007 in the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Texas, Marshall Division, alleging
infringement of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;7,065,417 entitled &#147;MPEG Portable Sound Reproducing System and A Reproducing Method Thereof.&#148; The complaint seeks unspecified damages and other relief. On July&nbsp;12, 2007, the Company filed a
petition for reexamination of the patent, which the U.S. Patent and Trademark Office granted. Plaintiff filed an amended complaint on August&nbsp;1, 2007, adding the iPhone as an accused device. On August&nbsp;2, 2007, the Company filed a motion to
stay the litigation pending the outcome of the reexamination, which the Court denied. The Company filed an answer on August&nbsp;20, 2007, denying all material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses. The Company also asserted
counterclaims for declaratory judgment of non-infringement and invalidity. The Markman hearing is set for March&nbsp;12, 2009, and trial is scheduled for July&nbsp;6, 2009. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>The Apple iPod iTunes Antitrust Litigation (formerly Charoensak v. Apple Computer, Inc. and Tucker v. Apple Computer, Inc.); Black v. Apple Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The first-listed action is a consolidated case combining two cases previously pending under the names <I>Charoensak v. Apple Computer Inc. (formerly
Slattery v. Apple Computer Inc.)</I> and <I>Tucker v. Apple Computer, Inc.</I> The original plaintiff (Slattery) in the Charoensak case filed a purported class action on January&nbsp;3, 2005 in the United States District Court for the Northern
District of California alleging various claims including alleged unlawful tying of music purchased on the iTunes Store with the purchase of iPods and unlawful acquisition or maintenance of monopoly market power. Plaintiff&#146;s complaint alleged
violations of &#167;&#167;1 and 2 of the Sherman Act (15 U.S.C. &#167;&#167;1 and 2), California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;16700 et seq. (the Cartwright Act), California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17200 (unfair
competition), common law unjust enrichment and common law monopolization. </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">36 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff sought unspecified damages and other relief. The Company filed a motion to dismiss on February&nbsp;10, 2005. On September&nbsp;9, 2005, the Court
denied the motion in part and granted it in part. Plaintiff filed an amended complaint on September&nbsp;23, 2005 and the Company filed an answer on October&nbsp;18, 2005. In August 2006, the Court dismissed Slattery without prejudice and allowed
plaintiffs to file an amended complaint naming two new plaintiffs (Charoensak and Rosen). On November&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company filed an answer to the amended complaint denying all material allegations and asserting numerous affirmative defenses.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Tucker case was filed as a purported class action on July&nbsp;21, 2006 in the United States District Court for the Northern District
of California alleging various claims including alleged unlawful tying of music and videos purchased on the iTunes Store with the purchase of iPods and vice versa and unlawful acquisition or maintenance of monopoly market power. The complaint
alleges violations of &#167;&#167;1 and 2 of the Sherman Act (15 U.S.C. &#167;&#167;1 and 2), California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;16700 et seq. (the Cartwright Act), California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17200
(unfair competition) and the California Consumer Legal Remedies Act. Plaintiff sought unspecified damages and other relief. On November&nbsp;3, 2006, the Company filed a motion to dismiss the complaint. On December&nbsp;20, 2006, the Court denied
the motion to dismiss. On January&nbsp;11, 2007, The Company filed an answer denying all material allegations and asserting numerous defenses. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">On March&nbsp;20, 2007, the Court consolidated the two cases. Plaintiffs filed a consolidated complaint on April&nbsp;19, 2007. On June&nbsp;6, 2007, the Company filed an answer to the consolidated complaint denying all material allegations
and asserting numerous affirmative defenses. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A related class action complaint, <I>Black v. Apple Inc</I>., was filed on August&nbsp;27,
2007 in the Circuit Court in Broward County, Florida, alleging that the Company is attempting to maintain a monopoly by precluding customers from using non-iTunes downloads on iPods and from using iTunes music on non-iPod MP3 players.&nbsp;Plaintiff
alleges that the Company&#146;s alleged monopolization violates the Florida Antitrust Act and the Florida Deceptive and Unfair Trade Practices Act.&nbsp;Plaintiff seeks unspecified damages and other relief.&nbsp;The Company removed the case to the
United States District Court for the Southern District of Florida on September&nbsp;28, 2007, and filed a motion to transfer the case to the Northern District of California on October&nbsp;12, 2007.&nbsp;The Company&#146;s motion to transfer was
granted on October&nbsp;17, 2007. Plaintiff and the Company entered into a Stipulation for Voluntary Dismissal on November&nbsp;19, 2007, and the Court entered plaintiff&#146;s dismissal of all claims with prejudice on November&nbsp;20, 2007. The
matter is concluded. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A related class action complaint, <I>Somers v. Apple Inc</I>., was filed on December&nbsp;31, 2007 in the United
States District Court for the Northern District of California, alleging various claims including alleged unlawful tying of music and videos purchased on the iTunes Store with the purchase of iPods and vice versa and unlawful acquisition or
maintenance of monopoly market power. The complaint alleges violations of &#167;&#167;1 and 2 of the Sherman Act (15 U.S.C. &#167;&#167;1 and 2), California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;16700 et seq. (the Cartwright Act), California
Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17200 (unfair competition) and the California Consumer Legal Remedies Act. Plaintiff seeks unspecified damages and other relief. The Company&#146;s response to the complaint is not yet due. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Tse v. Apple Computer, Inc. et al. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">Plaintiff Ho Keung Tse filed this action against the Company and other defendants on August&nbsp;5, 2005 in the United States District Court for the District of Maryland alleging infringement of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;6,665,797 entitled
&#147;Protection of Software Again [sic] Against Unauthorized Use.&#148; The complaint seeks unspecified damages and other relief. The Company filed an answer on October&nbsp;31, 2005 denying all material allegations and asserting numerous
affirmative defenses. On October&nbsp;28, 2005, the Company and the other defendants filed a motion to transfer the case to the Northern District of California, which was granted on August&nbsp;31, 2006. On July&nbsp;24, 2007, the Company filed a
petition for reexamination of the patent, which the U.S. Patent and Trademark Office granted. On July&nbsp;25, 2007, the Company filed a motion to stay the litigation pending the outcome of the reexamination, which the Court granted on
October&nbsp;4, 2007. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Union F&eacute;d&eacute;rale des Consummateurs - Que Choisir v. Apple Computer France S.&agrave;.r.l. and iTunes
S.&agrave;.r.l. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff, a consumer association in France, filed this complaint on February&nbsp;9, 2005 alleging that the
above-listed entities are violating consumer law by (1)&nbsp;omitting to mention that the iPod is allegedly not compatible with music from online music services other than the iTunes Store and that the music from the iTunes Store is only compatible
with the iPod and (2)&nbsp;allegedly tying the sales of iPods to the iTunes Store and vice versa. Plaintiff seeks damages, injunctive relief and other relief. The first hearing on the case took place on May&nbsp;24, 2005. The Company&#146;s response
to the complaint was served on November&nbsp;8, 2005. Plaintiff&#146;s responsive pleading was filed on February&nbsp;10, 2006. The Company filed a reply on June&nbsp;6, 2006 and UFC filed a response on September&nbsp;19, 2006. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">37 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Vitt v. Apple Computer, Inc. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed this purported class action on November&nbsp;7, 2006 in the United States District Court for the Central District of California on behalf of a purported nationwide class of all
purchasers of the iBook G4 alleging that the computer&#146;s logic board fails at an abnormally high rate. The complaint alleges violations of California Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17200 (unfair competition) and California
Business&nbsp;&amp; Professions Code &#167;17500 (false advertising). Plaintiff seeks unspecified damages and other relief. The Company filed a motion to dismiss on January&nbsp;19, 2007, which the Court granted on March&nbsp;13, 2007. Plaintiffs
filed an amended complaint on March&nbsp;26, 2007. The Company filed a motion to dismiss on August&nbsp;16, 2007, which was heard on October&nbsp;4, 2007. The Court has not yet issued a ruling. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Vogel v. Jobs et al. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Plaintiff filed
this purported class action on August&nbsp;24, 2006, in the United States District Court for the Northern District of California against the Company and certain of the Company&#146;s current and former officers and directors alleging improper
backdating of stock option grants to maximize certain defendants&#146; profits, failing to properly account for those grants and issuing false financial statements. On January&nbsp;19, 2007, the Court appointed the New York City Employees&#146;
Retirement System as lead plaintiff. On March&nbsp;23, 2007, plaintiffs&nbsp;filed a Consolidated Class Action Complaint. The&nbsp;Consolidated&nbsp;Complaint purports to be brought on behalf of several classes of holders of the Company&#146;s stock
and&nbsp;asserts claims under Section&nbsp;14(a) and 20(a) of the Securities Exchange Act&nbsp;as well as state law. The Consolidated Complaint seeks rescission of amendments to various stock option and other incentive compensation plans, an
accounting and damages in an unspecified amount. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss on June&nbsp;8, 2007, which was heard on September&nbsp;7, 2007. On November&nbsp;14, 2007, the Court issued an order dismissing all securities claims with
prejudice, and held that any amended complaint could only be styled as a derivative case. On December&nbsp;14, 2007, plaintiff filed a motion for leave to file a first amended consolidated class action complaint. On January 23, 2008, defendants
filed an opposition to plaintiff&#146;s motion for leave. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">38 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
